# LoCoBench-Agent Task

## Overview

**Task ID**: c_fintech_payment_expert_065_architectural_understanding_expert_01
**Category**: architectural_understanding
**Difficulty**: expert
**Language**: c
**Context Length**: 886345 tokens
**Files**: 75

## Task Title

Architectural Design for Cross-Service Tuition Auto-Payment

## Description

EduPay Ledger Academy is a sophisticated FinTech platform designed to manage all financial operations for a university. The system is built in C and employs a microservices architecture, with key services for the Bursar's Office (`bursar_service`) and the Financial Aid Office (`financial_aid_service`). The architecture heavily relies on advanced patterns including Clean Architecture, CQRS with Event Sourcing, and the Saga pattern for managing distributed transactions across services. A new feature is requested: 'Tuition Auto-Payment'. This feature should automatically apply a student's newly disbursed financial aid stipend towards their outstanding tuition balance, but only if the student has explicitly opted in. The challenge is to design a solution that seamlessly integrates this cross-service functionality while upholding the system's strict architectural principles of consistency, reliability, and regulatory compliance.

## Your Task

As a senior software architect for the EduPay Ledger Academy project, you are tasked with creating a detailed architectural proposal for the new 'Tuition Auto-Payment' feature. Your proposal should be a technical markdown document that outlines how to implement this feature without violating the existing architectural patterns.

Your proposal must address the following points:

1.  **Interaction Diagram/Sequence:** Describe the step-by-step flow of communication between the `financial_aid_service`, the `bursar_service`, and any other relevant components. Detail the sequence of commands, events, and queries.
2.  **Saga Pattern Integration:** Explain how the Saga pattern will be used to manage the distributed transaction. Will you extend an existing saga (like the one in `disburse_stipend_saga.c`) or create a new one? Justify your choice and describe the saga's steps, including any necessary compensating actions.
3.  **New Domain Events:** Define the new domain events required for this feature (e.g., for successful application, failure, etc.). Specify which service would publish these events and which services would consume them.
4.  **CQRS/Event Sourcing Impact:** Detail how this new workflow will be recorded in the event store. Explain which aggregates in the `bursar_service` (e.g., `Account`, `Ledger`) would be affected. Also, describe how the `projections_service` would need to be updated to reflect these auto-payments in its read models (e.g., for student dashboards).
5.  **Compliance and Consent:** Referencing the principles in `docs/architecture/05_security_and_compliance.md` and `docs/lessons/L03_Regulatory_Compliance_in_Code.md`, explain how your design handles the student's opt-in consent. Where would this consent flag be stored and how would it be checked in the workflow?
6.  **Affected Components:** List the key files and components (e.g., specific use cases, handlers, domain models, infrastructure) that would require modification to implement your design.

## Expected Approach

An expert developer would begin by thoroughly reviewing the existing architecture documentation, especially `02_microservices_and_bounded_contexts.md`, `03_cqrs_and_event_sourcing.md`, and `04_saga_pattern.md`. They would recognize that this is a classic distributed transaction problem perfectly suited for the existing Saga pattern.

The developer would inspect `financial_aid_service/application/use_cases/disburse_stipend_saga.c` to understand how stipends are currently processed. They would identify that the `StipendDisbursed` event, published via RabbitMQ (`rabbitmq_publisher.c`), is the logical trigger for the new functionality.

Their proposed design would likely extend the existing `DisburseStipendSaga` rather than creating a new one, arguing that applying funds to tuition is part of the overall stipend disbursement process. This keeps the transaction context unified.

The proposal would outline a new step in the saga that occurs after the stipend is successfully disbursed. This step would issue a command, like `ApplyStipendToTuition`, to the `bursar_service`. Before issuing the command, the saga coordinator would first need to query a read model to check for two conditions: (1) the student's opt-in status and (2) an outstanding balance. This query would target a projection maintained by the `projections_service` or a query endpoint on the `bursar_service`.

The design would define new events like `StipendAppliedToTuition` and `StipendApplicationToTuitionFailed`. It would also define a compensating action, `ReverseTuitionApplication`, for the saga in case a subsequent step fails.

Finally, the developer would trace the impact through the system: the `bursar_service` command handler would update the `Account` and `Ledger` aggregates, persisting the new events to the `postgres_event_store`. The `projections_service` would need a new event handler in a file like `dashboard_projector.c` to consume the `StipendAppliedToTuition` event and update the student's account balance projection.

## Evaluation Criteria

- **Pattern Adherence:** Correctly identifies and proposes extending the existing Saga pattern, respecting the CQRS/ES flow.
- **Component Identification:** Accurately identifies the roles of `financial_aid_service`, `bursar_service`, `projections_service`, and the Saga Coordinator.
- **Data Flow Correctness:** Proposes a logical and correct sequence of events, commands, and queries, including the crucial pre-condition check.
- **Event Design:** Defines specific and meaningful new domain events appropriate for the feature.
- **Compliance Integration:** Explicitly addresses the student consent requirement and correctly places the check in the workflow, referencing the compliance documentation.
- **Codebase Awareness:** Demonstrates understanding of the codebase by correctly identifying key files/modules that would need modification (e.g., `disburse_stipend_saga.c`, `dashboard_projector.c`).
- **Justification Quality:** Provides clear reasoning for architectural decisions, such as choosing to extend the existing saga versus creating a new one.

     9ŌåÆ

    11ŌåÆ> ŌĆö EduPay Core Team
    12ŌåÆ
    13ŌåÆEduPay Ledger Academy employs **CQRS** to divide **mutations** (Commands) from **reads** (Queries) so that educators can swap persistence technologies, message buses, or reporting databases without touching domain logic.   
    14ŌåÆAll state-changing requests are persisted as **immutable domain events**, enabling deterministic replay, powerful audit trails, and student-friendly time-travel debugging.

    38ŌåÆ**Projection / Read Model** | A denormalized view optimized for reads: dashboards, ledgers, etc.

     3ŌåÆ### docs/architecture/04_saga_pattern.md
     4ŌåÆ---

     8ŌåÆ> Status: Ō£ģ Production  
     9ŌåÆ---
    10ŌåÆ
    11ŌåÆ## 1. Why EduPay Uses the Saga Pattern
    12ŌåÆ
    13ŌåÆEduPay processes **millions of distributed, financial micro-transactions** each semester.  
    14ŌåÆThe platform deliberately avoids *single-phase* database transactions because:
    15ŌåÆ
    16ŌåÆ* **Micro-services** compose payments from multiple bounded contexts (Admissions, Bursar, Treasury, FX, Fraud).  
    17ŌåÆ* **Heterogeneous data stores** (PostgreSQL, Redis, EventStoreDB) participate in a single business flow.  
    18ŌåÆ* **Resiliency labs** in coursework require controlled failure injection and roll-back.  
    19ŌåÆ
    20ŌåÆA **Saga** slices a long-running business process into a series of *local* ACID transactions plus **compensating steps**.  
    21ŌåÆIf any step fails, the orchestrator triggers rollback actions in **reverse order**, yielding *eventual consistency* without locking global resources.
    22ŌåÆ
    23ŌåÆ```
    24ŌåÆEnrollment_Fee ŌåÆ FX_Conversion ŌåÆ Treasury_Posting ŌåÆ Fraud_Scoring ŌåÆ Receipt_Email
    25ŌåÆ         Ōöé                Ōöé                Ōöé              Ōöé
    26ŌåÆ         ŌööŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌö┤ŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌö┤ŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌö┤ŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöÉ
    27ŌåÆ                       Saga Orchestrator (payment_saga.c)       Ōöé
    28ŌåÆ                       ŌĆó persists state in Audit_Trail          Ōöé
    29ŌåÆ                       ŌĆó broadcasts events over EventBus        Ōöé

     1ŌåÆ# Lesson 03 ŌĆō Regulatory Compliance in Code
     2ŌåÆEduPay Ledger Academy ŌöĆ Bounded Context: Compliance

     4ŌåÆ
     5ŌåÆ> ŌĆ£Security and privacy requirements **are** business requirements.ŌĆØ

     7ŌåÆ
     8ŌåÆ---
     9ŌåÆ
    10ŌåÆ## ­¤¦Ł Learning objectives
    11ŌåÆ* Design code paths that meet FERPA, PCI-DSS v4.0 and PSD2 RTS.
    12ŌåÆ* Implement format-preserving tokenisation that keeps BIN analytics intact.
    13ŌåÆ* Encrypt audit-trail entries with AES-256-GCM while preserving CQRS read-models.
    14ŌåÆ* Shred secrets from RAM so students can pass a post-mortem memory scan.

    18ŌåÆ## 1 ŌĢ▒ 4ŌĆāHeader-only API surface (`compliance_guard.h`)

     1ŌåÆ/**
     2ŌåÆ * @file account.h
     3ŌåÆ *
     4ŌåÆ * @brief  Domain Model:  Bursar ŌĆæ Ledger Account Aggregate
     5ŌåÆ *
     6ŌåÆ * The Account aggregate is the canonical representation of a studentŌĆÖs financial
     7ŌåÆ * ledger inside the Bursar bounded-context.  It is intentionally persistence-agnostic
     8ŌåÆ * (Clean Architecture) and contains only business rules.  Orchestration with
     9ŌåÆ * payments gateways, SQL/NoSQL stores, or message brokers is delegated to the
    10ŌåÆ * outer ŌĆ£infrastructureŌĆØ layer.
    11ŌåÆ *
    12ŌåÆ * Thread-Safety:
    13ŌåÆ *  ŌĆō All mutating functions receive a pointer to the aggregate instance and MUST
    14ŌåÆ *    be protected by the calling applicationŌĆÖs concurrency strategy
    15ŌåÆ *    (mutex, actor model, etc.).  The domain layer purposefully remains
    16ŌåÆ *    synchronization-free to avoid bleeding implementation details inward.
    17ŌåÆ *
    18ŌåÆ * Monetary Representation:
    19ŌåÆ *  ŌĆō Amounts are stored as signed 64-bit integers representing the smallest
    20ŌåÆ *    denomination (ŌĆ£minor unitsŌĆØ, e.g. cents) to avoid floating-point error.
    21ŌåÆ *  ŌĆō The currency is an ISO-4217 alpha code held in a fixed-length char array.
    22ŌåÆ *
    23ŌåÆ * Copyright ┬® 2024
    24ŌåÆ * EduPay Ledger Academy ŌĆō All rights reserved.
    25ŌåÆ */
    26ŌåÆ
    27ŌåÆ#ifndef EDUPAY_LEDGER_ACADEMY_BURSAR_ACCOUNT_H
    28ŌåÆ#define EDUPAY_LEDGER_ACADEMY_BURSAR_ACCOUNT_H
    29ŌåÆ

     1ŌåÆ/**
     2ŌåÆ * @file ledger.h
     3ŌåÆ * @author
     4ŌåÆ *   EduPay Ledger Academy ŌĆö Bursar Service
     5ŌåÆ *
     6ŌåÆ * @brief Domain-level abstractions for the immutable double-entry ledger
     7ŌåÆ *        maintained by the Bursar bounded-context.
     8ŌåÆ *
     9ŌåÆ * The Ledger component is *framework-agnostic* and contains **no** references
    10ŌåÆ * to databases, loggers, message brokers or HTTP frameworks.  This guarantees
    11ŌåÆ * that students can swap infrastructure while the core business rules remain
    12ŌåÆ * stableŌĆöa key property of Robert C. MartinŌĆÖs Clean Architecture.
    13ŌåÆ *
    14ŌåÆ * All monetary calculations use fixed-precision integers (minor units) to avoid
    15ŌåÆ * floating-point rounding errors.  ISO-4217 alpha-3 currency codes are used
    16ŌåÆ * for multi-currency support.
    17ŌåÆ *
    18ŌåÆ * Conventions
    19ŌåÆ * -----------
    20ŌåÆ * ŌĆó All functions return 0 on success, non-zero `ledger_err_t` codes on failure.  
    21ŌåÆ * ŌĆó ŌĆ£ImmutableŌĆØ means _append-only_; once an entry is POSTED it can only be
    22ŌåÆ *   compensated by a REVERSAL entryŌĆönever mutated in place.  
    23ŌåÆ * ŌĆó Thread-safety: read-only operations are lock-free; mutating operations
    24ŌåÆ *   require the caller to provide a concurrency control strategy (e.g. external
    25ŌåÆ *   mutex, optimistic CAS or sequential command bus).
    26ŌåÆ */

     1ŌåÆ/*
     2ŌåÆ * EduPay Ledger Academy
     3ŌåÆ * File: projections_service/event_handlers/dashboard_projector.c
     4ŌåÆ *
     5ŌåÆ * Description:
     6ŌåÆ *   Dashboard projector responsible for building the real-time read-model that
     7ŌåÆ *   powers the instructor/student analytics dashboard.  The projector consumes
     8ŌåÆ *   immutable domain events from the event-bus and updates aggregated KPIŌĆÖs
     9ŌåÆ *   such as total tuition collected, payment counts, pending settlements, and
    10ŌåÆ *   open fraud alerts.  The component is written in C following Clean
    11ŌåÆ *   Architecture guidelines so that higher layers (REST, gRPC, GraphQL, etc.)
    12ŌåÆ *   can query the materialized view without coupling to the write-side or to
    13ŌåÆ *   any framework.
    14ŌåÆ *
    15ŌåÆ *   The projection state is persisted to a pluggable store; a lightweight
    16ŌåÆ *   POSIX-file implementation is provided for coursework convenience but can be
    17ŌåÆ *   replaced with SQLite, Redis, or cloud storage by swapping the v-table.
    18ŌåÆ *
    19ŌåÆ *   Thread-safety is guaranteed via a coarse mutex because projections are
    20ŌåÆ *   write-heavy and latency-tolerant relative to OLTP processing.
    21ŌåÆ *
    22ŌåÆ * Author: EduPay Core Engineering Team
    23ŌåÆ */

     1ŌåÆ/**
     2ŌåÆ * @file saga_coordinator.h
     3ŌåÆ *
     4ŌåÆ * @brief Core abstraction for orchestrating distributed transactions
     5ŌåÆ *        via the Saga Pattern inside EduPay Ledger Academy.
     6ŌåÆ *
     7ŌåÆ *  The coordinator lives in the domain layer (Enterprise-Business Rules)
     8ŌåÆ *  and therefore must not import any framework-specific headers.
     9ŌåÆ *  It exposes a small surface-area in C so that professors can swap
    10ŌåÆ *  infrastructure (Kafka, NATS, gRPC, REST, SQL, NoSQL, etc.) without
    11ŌåÆ *  recompiling core business rules.
    12ŌåÆ *
    13ŌåÆ *  Thread-safety:
    14ŌåÆ *      All public functions are re-entrant but *not* thread-safe.
    15ŌåÆ *      Callers that share a coordinator instance *must* provide their own
    16ŌåÆ *      synchronization (e.g., inject a mutex from the application layer).
    17ŌåÆ *
    18ŌåÆ *  Memory-management:
    19ŌåÆ *      Memory is allocated only inside saga_coordinator_create().
    20ŌåÆ *      The caller is responsible for releasing resources via
    21ŌåÆ *      saga_coordinator_destroy().
    22ŌåÆ *
    23ŌåÆ *  License:
    24ŌåÆ *      MIT ŌĆō Copyright ┬® 2024 EduPay Ledger Academy
    25ŌåÆ */
    26ŌåÆ
    27ŌåÆ#ifndef EDU_PAY_LEDGER_ACADEMY_CORE_SAGA_COORDINATOR_H
    28ŌåÆ#define EDU_PAY_LEDGER_ACADEMY_CORE_SAGA_COORDINATOR_H
    29ŌåÆ
    30ŌåÆ/*------------------------------ System Headers -----------------------------*/

     2ŌåÆ * @file get_account_balance_query.h

     4ŌåÆ * @brief Application-layer query for retrieving the current ledger balance

    32ŌåÆ *      }

86-assistanttext-
I have completed the comprehensive architectural proposal for the Tuition Auto-Payment feature. The solution has been written to `/logs/agent/solution.md`.

## Summary of the Proposal

The architectural proposal addresses all required points:

### 1. Interaction Diagram/Sequence
- Detailed 10-step flow showing communication between `financial_aid_service`, `bursar_service`, `projections_service`, and the Saga Coordinator
- Includes the critical eligibility query before issuing the auto-payment command

### 2. Saga Pattern Integration
- **Recommendation**: Extend the existing `DisburseStipendSaga` (in `disburse_stipend_saga.c:367-372`) rather than creating a new saga
- **Justification**: Maintains transaction unity since auto-payment is logically part of stipend disbursement
- Added a new step `APPLY_TO_TUITION` with its compensating action `compensate_apply_to_tuition`

### 3. New Domain Events
- `StipendAppliedToTuition` - Published by `bursar_service` on successful application
- `StipendApplicationToTuitionFailed` - Published on failure for monitoring
- `AutoPaymentConsentChanged` - Published when student consent changes

### 4. CQRS/Event Sourcing Impact
- **Account Aggregate** (`account.h`): New `account_credit_from_stipend()` method
- **Ledger Aggregate** (`ledger.h`): New entry type `LEDGER_ENTRY_STIPEND_TO_TUITION`
- **Projections**: Updated `dashboard_projector.c` to handle new events, plus a new `student_balance_projector.c`

### 5. Compliance and Consent
- Referenced `05_security_and_compliance.md` and `L03_Regulatory_Compliance_in_Code.md`
- Consent stored as a first-class domain entity with full audit trail
- Consent check is explicitly gated in the saga workflow before any auto-payment occurs

Other contexts (Financial-Aid,\n  Continuing-Education) subscribe to project read models.\n*/\n#include <stdint.h>\n#include <time.h>\n\n#define PAYMENT_AUTH_VERSION 1\n\ntypedef struct ep_payment_auth_t {\n    uint8_t  version;          /* schema version                     */\n    char     id[37];           /* UUID v4 string                     */\n    char     student_id[16];   /* canonical SID                      */\n    char     invoice_id[37];   /* payment belongs to which invoice   */\n    char     currency[4];      /* ISO-4217                           */\n    int64_t  amount_minor;     /* 1099 = $10.99 ( if cents )         */\n    char     auth_code[12];    /* provided by payment processor      */\n    time_t   occurred_at_utc;  /* RFC 3339 ts                        */\n} ep_payment_auth_t;\n\n#endif /* EP_EVENTS_PAYMENT_AUTH_H */\n```\n\n## Service Skeleton: `ledger-core`\n\nThe canonical micro-service exposes gRPC, publishes events on NATS,\nand persists to PostgreSQL.  Internally, Clean Architecture layers are\nsegregated into `domain`, `usecase`, and `infra` directories.\n\n### `domain/money.h`\n\n```c\n/* domain/money.h */\n#ifndef EP_DOMAIN_MONEY_H\n#define EP_DOMAIN_MONEY_H\n\n#include <stdint.h>\n\ntypedef struct ep_money_t {\n    int64_t amount_minor;  /* -922337203685477 */\n    char    currency[4];   /* \"USD\"            */\n} ep_money_t;\n\n/* Equality check without floating-point errors */\nstatic inline int ep_money_eq(const ep_money_t *a, const ep_money_t *b)\n{\n    return a && b &&\n           a->amount_minor == b->amount_minor &&\n           a->currency[0] == b->currency[0] &&\n           a->currency[1] == b->currency[1] &&\n           a->currency[2] == b->currency[2] &&\n           a->currency[3] == b->currency[3];\n}\n\n#endif /* EP_DOMAIN_MONEY_H */\n```\n\n### `usecase/post_payment.c`\n\n```c\n/* usecase/post_payment.c */\n#include \"domain/money.h\"\n#include \"events/payment_authorized.h\"\n#include <stdio.h>\n#include <string.h>\n\ntypedef struct ep_payment_repo ep_payment_repo_t;\ntypedef struct ep_event_bus   ep_event_bus_t;\n\n/* Dependency inversion via pure C interfaces */\nstruct ep_payment_repo {\n    int (*begin_tx)(ep_payment_repo_t *);\n    int (*commit_tx)(ep_payment_repo_t *);\n    int (*rollback_tx)(ep_payment_repo_t *);\n    int (*insert_ledger_entry)(ep_payment_repo_t *,\n                               const char  *invoice_id,\n                               const ep_money_t *amount,\n                               const char  *auth_code);\n};\n\nstruct ep_event_bus {\n    int (*publish)(ep_event_bus_t *, const void *evt, size_t sz);\n};\n\n/*\n  Post a payment to the double-entry ledger.\n\n  Returns 0 on success, < 0 on domain error, > 0 on infra error.\n*/\nint ep_uc_post_payment(ep_payment_repo_t *repo,\n                       ep_event_bus_t    *bus,\n                       const char        *invoice_id,\n                       const ep_money_t  *amount,\n                       const char        *auth_code)\n{\n    if (!repo || !bus || !invoice_id || !amount || !auth_code)\n        return -1; /* pre-condition failed */\n\n    if (repo->begin_tx(repo) != 0)\n        return  1; /* infra error */\n\n    if (repo->insert_ledger_entry(repo, invoice_id, amount, auth_code) != 0) {\n        repo->rollback_tx(repo);\n        return  2;\n    }\n\n    ep_payment_auth_t evt = {\n        .version        = PAYMENT_AUTH_VERSION,\n        .occurred_at_utc= time(NULL),\n    };\n    /* (Safe) string copy utilities omitted for brevity */\n    strncpy(evt.id,        \"UUID-GEN-STUB\", sizeof evt.id);\n    strncpy(evt.student_id,\"SID-LOOKUP-X\", sizeof evt.student_id);\n    strncpy(evt.invoice_id,invoice_id,     sizeof evt.invoice_id);\n    strncpy(evt.currency,  amount->currency, sizeof evt.currency);\n    evt.amount_minor = amount->amount_minor;\n    strncpy(evt.auth_code, auth_code, sizeof evt.auth_code);\n\n    if (bus->publish(bus, &evt, sizeof evt) != 0) {\n        repo->rollback_tx(repo);\n        return  3;\n    }\n\n    return repo->commit_tx(repo);\n}\n```\n\n### Saga Orchestrator (Distributed Tuition Payment)\n\n```c\n/* saga/tuition_payment_saga.h */\n#ifndef EP_SAGA_TUITION_PAYMENT_H\n#define EP_SAGA_TUITION_PAYMENT_H\n\n/*\n  TuitionPaymentSaga orchestrates:\n\n  1. Reserve Financial-Aid budget\n  2. Authorize card payment (Bursar)\n  3. Disburse stipends\n  4. Issue micro-credential revenue split\n\n  Compensation order is reverse.\n\n  State machine is stored in the EventStore; students step through\n  failures during outage simulations.\n*/\n\ntypedef enum {\n    SAGA_STEP_NONE = 0,\n    SAGA_STEP_AID_RESERVED,\n    SAGA_STEP_PAYMENT_AUTHORIZED,\n    SAGA_STEP_STIPEND_PAID,\n    SAGA_STEP_MICROCRED_SPLIT,\n    SAGA_STEP_DONE,\n    SAGA_STEP_FAILED\n} ep_saga_state_t;\n\n#endif /* EP_SAGA_TUITION_PAYMENT_H */\n```\n\n## Anti-corruption Layer (ACL) Sample\n\nAdmissions uses an external vendor for SIS and must translate its JSON\nschema into *StudentRegistered* events.\n\n```c\n/* acl/sis_adapter.c */\n#include <jansson.h>\n#include \"events/student_registered.h\"\n\n/* Returns 0 on success */\nint ep_acl_translate_sis_event(const char *json,\n                               ep_student_reg_t *out_evt)\n{\n    json_error_t err;\n    json_t *root = json_loads(json, 0, &err);\n    if (!root) return -1;\n\n    const char *sid   = json_string_value(json_object_get(root, \"sid\"));\n    const char *email = json_string_value(json_object_get(root, \"email\"));\n    if (!sid || !email) {\n        json_decref(root);\n        return -2;\n    }\n\n    strncpy(out_evt->student_id, sid, sizeof out_evt->student_id);\n    strncpy(out_evt->email,      email, sizeof out_evt->email);\n    out_evt->occurred_at_utc = time(NULL);\n\n    json_decref(root);\n    return 0;\n}\n```\n\n## Data Ownership & ACID Boundaries\n\n* **Admissions** owns `Student` aggregate; others reference via SID.\n* **Ledger-core** owns `Invoice`, `LedgerEntry`.\n* **Financial-Aid** owns `Award`, `AidDisbursement`.\n* Shared Kernel\u2019s `AuditTrail` is append-only; no service can mutate.\n\n| Service        | DB Schema          | Tx Boundary (Local ACID)    |\n|----------------|--------------------|-----------------------------|\n| admissions     | `admissions.*`     | `Student`, `Applicant`      |\n| ledger-core    | `ledger.*`         | `Invoice`, `LedgerEntry`    |\n| aid-engine     | `aid.*`            | `Award`, `Disbursement`     |\n| micro-cred     | `microcred.*`      | `CourseRun`, `SplitPayout`  |\n\n## Resilience Policy\n\n1. Idempotent command handlers.\n2. At-least-once event delivery (NATS JetStream).\n3. Circuit-breaker around external PSP, open after 3 failures / 30 s.\n4. Saga compensation for inter-context failure.\n\n```c\n/* infra/circuit_breaker.h */\n#ifndef EP_INFRA_CIRCUIT_BREAKER_H\n#define EP_INFRA_CIRCUIT_BREAKER_H\n#include <time.h>\ntypedef enum { CB_CLOSED, CB_OPEN, CB_HALF_OPEN } cb_state_t;\n\ntypedef struct circuit_breaker {\n    cb_state_t state;\n    unsigned   failure_count;\n    time_t     last_failure;\n    unsigned   open_timeout_sec;\n    unsigned   threshold;\n} circuit_breaker_t;\n\nvoid cb_init(circuit_breaker_t *cb,\n             unsigned threshold,\n             unsigned open_timeout_sec);\n\nint  cb_before_request(circuit_breaker_t *cb);\nvoid cb_after_success(circuit_breaker_t *cb);\nvoid cb_after_failure(circuit_breaker_t *cb);\n\n#endif /* EP_INFRA_CIRCUIT_BREAKER_H */\n```\n\n## Build & Deployment Standards\n\n* `Dockerfile` uses scratch + `musl-clang` static linking \u21d2 6 MB images.\n* Each service exports `/livez` and `/readyz` over HTTP on port 8080.\n* Kubernetes Helm charts pin CPU/memory, configure HPA on NATS lag.\n\n---\n\n> \u201cArchitecture is about the important stuff\u2014whatever that is.\u201d  \n> \u2014 Ralph Johnson\n\nLearners should fork this repository, enable **Saga Pattern\nDemonstration Mode** (`make chaos-on`), and trigger the `tuition\ncheckout` flow. Domain Vocabulary  \n2. High Level Flow Diagram  \n3. Command Pipeline (Write Model)  \n4. Event Store Implementation (C)  \n5. Query Model & Projections  \n6. Consistency, Concurrency, and Idempotency  \n7. Failure Injection Labs  \n8. Further Reading\n\n---\n\n## 1. Domain Vocabulary\n\nTerm | Definition\n---- | ----------\n**Command** | An intent _to do_ something. Must either succeed or return an error.\n**Event** | A fact _that something happened_. Can never change or be removed.\n**Aggregate** | A transactional consistency boundary, e.g., `LedgerAccount`.\n**Projection / Read Model** | A denormalized view optimized for reads: dashboards, ledgers, etc.\n\n---\n\n## 2. High Level Flow Diagram\n\n```mermaid\nsequenceDiagram\n    actor Student\n    participant CMD as Command API\n    participant CH as Command Handler\n    participant ES as Event Store (append-only)\n    participant PR as Projector\n    participant RM as Read Model (SQLite)\n    Student->>CMD: POST /accounts/deposit\n    CMD->>CH: DepositFundsCommand\n    CH->>ES: Append(EventDeposited)\n    ES->>PR: Emit(EventDeposited)\n    PR->>RM: UPDATE balances\n    Student->>RM: GET /dashboard\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. Command Pipeline (Write Model)\n\nBelow is a **compile-ready** excerpt (C17) showing how a `CommandBus` validates and dispatches commands to their handlers.  \nIt purposefully decouples IO so professors can mock the bus during unit tests.\n\n```c\n/* File: src/cqrs/command_bus.h */\n#ifndef EDU_PAY_COMMAND_BUS_H\n#define EDU_PAY_COMMAND_BUS_H\n\n#include <stdint.h>\n#include <stddef.h>\n#include \"utils/uuid.h\"\n\n/* ---------- Generic Command Definition ---------- */\ntypedef struct {\n    uuid_t   id;         /* Correlation ID for tracing */\n    uint64_t timestamp;  /* epoch millis (monotonic)   */\n    const char *type;    /* \"DepositFundsCommand\" etc  */\n    void     *payload;   /* domain-specific struct ptr */\n} command_t;\n\n/* Error codes follow POSIX semantics for reuse in shell scripts */\ntypedef enum {\n    CMD_OK          = 0,\n    CMD_ERR_INPUT   = 22,  /* EINVAL */\n    CMD_ERR_HANDLER = 38,  /* ENOSYS */\n    CMD_ERR_REJECT  = 35   /* EDEADLK \u2013 business rule violated */\n} command_status_e;\n\n/* Opaque route handle resolves to specific handler at runtime */\ntypedef command_status_e (*command_handler_f)(const command_t *cmd);\n\n/* Register handler */\nint command_bus_register(const char *type, command_handler_f fn);\n\n/* Dispatch (synchronous) */\ncommand_status_e command_bus_execute(const command_t *cmd);\n\n#endif /* EDU_PAY_COMMAND_BUS_H */\n```\n\n```c\n/* File: src/cqrs/command_bus.c */\n#include \"cqrs/command_bus.h\"\n#include <stdlib.h>\n#include <string.h>\n#include \"utils/hashtable.h\"\n\n/* --- Very light associative table (string \u2192 function ptr) --- */\nstatic hash_table_t *router = NULL;\n\nint command_bus_register(const char *type, command_handler_f fn) {\n    if (!type || !fn) return -CMD_ERR_INPUT;\n    if (!router) router = ht_create(32);\n    return ht_put(router, type, fn);\n}\n\ncommand_status_e command_bus_execute(const command_t *cmd) {\n    if (!cmd || !cmd->type) return CMD_ERR_INPUT;\n    command_handler_f fn = ht_get(router, cmd->type);\n    if (!fn) return CMD_ERR_HANDLER;\n    return fn(cmd);\n}\n```\n\nExample Domain Command + Handler:\n\n```c\n/* File: src/payments/commands/deposit_funds.h */\n#ifndef EDU_PAY_COMMAND_DEPOSIT_H\n#define EDU_PAY_COMMAND_DEPOSIT_H\n#include <stdint.h>\n\ntypedef struct {\n    char     account_id[36];\n    uint64_t amount_cents;\n    char     currency[4];        /* \"USD\" | \"EUR\" | etc. */\n} deposit_funds_payload_t;\n\n#endif\n```\n\n```c\n/* File: src/payments/handlers/deposit_funds_handler.c */\n#include \"cqrs/command_bus.h\"\n#include \"events/event_bus.h\"\n#include \"payments/commands/deposit_funds.h\"\n#include \"payments/events/funds_deposited.h\"\n#include \"domain/accounts_repository.h\"\n#include \"utils/clock.h\"\n#include \"utils/currency.h\"\n\nstatic command_status_e handle_deposit(const command_t *cmd)\n{\n    if (!cmd || !cmd->payload) return CMD_ERR_INPUT;\n    const deposit_funds_payload_t *pl = cmd->payload;\n\n    /* --- Business Rule Enforcement --- */\n    if (!currency_is_supported(pl->currency) || pl->amount_cents == 0)\n        return CMD_ERR_REJECT;\n\n    /* Optimistic lock fetch */\n    ledger_account_t acct;\n    if (accounts_repo_load(pl->account_id, &acct) != 0)\n        return CMD_ERR_REJECT; /* Unknown account */\n\n    /* Domain invariants can run here (e.g., AML limits) */\n    /* ... */\n\n    /* --- Produce Event (immutably) --- */\n    funds_deposited_event_t ev = {\n        .base.id        = uuid_v4(),\n        .base.timestamp = clock_epoch_ms(),\n        .base.type      = \"FundsDepositedEvent\",\n        .account_id     = {0},\n        .amount_cents   = pl->amount_cents,\n        .currency       = {0}\n    };\n    strncpy(ev.account_id, pl->account_id, sizeof(ev.account_id)-1);\n    strncpy(ev.currency, pl->currency,   sizeof(ev.currency)-1);\n\n    /* Persist via Event Bus (which writes through to Event Store) */\n    if (event_bus_publish((event_t *)&ev) != EVT_OK)\n        return CMD_ERR_HANDLER;\n\n    return CMD_OK;\n}\n\n/* Auto-register at startup */\n__attribute__((constructor))\nstatic void _deposit_register(void) {\n    command_bus_register(\"DepositFundsCommand\", handle_deposit);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Event Store Implementation (C)\n\nThe **Event Store** is append-only, leverages `mmap(2)` for re-play speed, and stores each record as length-prefixed JSON so that students can grep logs with *jq*.\n\n```c\n/* File: src/event_store/event_store.h */\n#ifndef EDU_PAY_EVENT_STORE_H\n#define EDU_PAY_EVENT_STORE_H\n\n#include <stddef.h>\n#include <stdint.h>\n#include \"events/event.h\"\n\n#define EVT_STORE_OK          0\n#define EVT_STORE_ERR_IO    (-5)\n#define EVT_STORE_ERR_FULL (-28)    /* ENOSPC */\n\n/* Append single event (thread-safe, fsync\u2019ed) */\nint event_store_append(const event_t *ev);\n\n/* Stream all events for replay (blocking). \n   Calls `callback` for each event; stop when it returns non-zero. */\ntypedef int (*event_stream_cb)(const event_t *ev, void *ctx);\nint event_store_stream(event_stream_cb callback, void *ctx);\n\n#endif\n```\n\n```c\n/* File: src/event_store/event_store.c */\n#define _POSIX_C_SOURCE 200809L\n#include \"event_store/event_store.h\"\n#include <fcntl.h>\n#include <sys/mman.h>\n#include <sys/stat.h>\n#include <unistd.h>\n#include <pthread.h>\n#include <stdio.h>\n#include <string.h>\n#include \"utils/serialize_json.h\"\n#include \"utils/spinlock.h\"\n\n#define EVENT_STORE_FILE \"./var/event_store.log\"\n#define MAX_EVENT_SIZE   4096   /* hard cap to aid undergrad sanity */\n\nstatic int fd = -1;\nstatic pthread_spinlock_t lock;\n\n__attribute__((constructor))\nstatic void _init_store(void) {\n    fd = open(EVENT_STORE_FILE, O_RDWR | O_CREAT | O_APPEND, 0640);\n    pthread_spin_init(&lock, PTHREAD_PROCESS_PRIVATE);\n}\n\n__attribute__((destructor))\nstatic void _close_store(void) {\n    if (fd != -1) close(fd);\n    pthread_spin_destroy(&lock);\n}\n\nint event_store_append(const event_t *ev)\n{\n    if (!ev) return EVT_STORE_ERR_IO;\n\n    char buffer[MAX_EVENT_SIZE];\n    ssize_t len = json_serialize_event(ev, buffer, sizeof(buffer));\n    if (len < 0) return EVT_STORE_ERR_IO;\n\n    /* Length-prefixed frame */\n    uint32_t nlen = (uint32_t)len;\n    pthread_spin_lock(&lock);\n    ssize_t w = write(fd, &nlen, sizeof(nlen));\n    w += write(fd, buffer, len);\n    fsync(fd);\n    pthread_spin_unlock(&lock);\n\n    return (w == (ssize_t)(sizeof(nlen) + len)) ? EVT_STORE_OK\n                                                : EVT_STORE_ERR_IO;\n}\n\nint event_store_stream(event_stream_cb cb, void *ctx)\n{\n    if (!cb) return EVT_STORE_ERR_IO;\n\n    int sfd = open(EVENT_STORE_FILE, O_RDONLY);\n    if (sfd < 0) return EVT_STORE_ERR_IO;\n\n    uint32_t nlen;\n    while (read(sfd, &nlen, sizeof(nlen)) == sizeof(nlen)) {\n        if (nlen > MAX_EVENT_SIZE) { close(sfd); return EVT_STORE_ERR_IO; }\n        char buffer[MAX_EVENT_SIZE];\n        if (read(sfd, buffer, nlen) != (ssize_t)nlen) break;\n\n        event_t *ev = json_deserialize_event(buffer, nlen);\n        if (!ev) continue;\n        if (cb(ev, ctx) != 0) { free(ev); break; }\n        free(ev);\n    }\n    close(sfd);\n    return EVT_STORE_OK;\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Query Model & Projections\n\nRead models are **eventually consistent**. Every event published above is fanned-out to one or more *Projectors* that transform it into query-optimized databases (SQLite, Redis, CSV for Excel labs).\n\n```c\n/* File: src/projections/balance_projection.c */\n#include \"events/event_bus.h\"\n#include \"payments/events/funds_deposited.h\"\n#include \"database/sqlite.h\"\n\nstatic int on_funds_deposited(const event_t *ev)\n{\n    const funds_deposited_event_t *e = (const funds_deposited_event_t *)ev;\n    return sqlite_exec(\n        \"INSERT INTO account_balance(account_id, currency, balance_cents) \"\n        \"VALUES (?1, ?2, ?3) \"\n        \"ON CONFLICT(account_id, currency) \"\n        \"DO UPDATE SET balance_cents = balance_cents + excluded.balance_cents;\",\n        e->account_id, e->currency, (int64_t)e->amount_cents);\n}\n\n__attribute__((constructor))\nstatic void _register_projector(void) {\n    event_bus_subscribe(\"FundsDepositedEvent\", on_funds_deposited);\n}\n```\n\nStudents can query via the REST shell or `sqlite3 var/read_models.db`.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Consistency, Concurrency, and Idempotency\n\n\u2022 **Concurrency Control** \u2013 Each aggregate carries a monotonically increasing `version`. Handlers pass the expected `version` into `event_store_append()`.  \n\u2022 **At-Least-Once Delivery** \u2013 Projectors keep an `offset` table so they can re-play events idempotently.  \n\u2022 **Snap-Shots** \u2013 Long-lived aggregates (>2 000 events) periodically persist snapshots to avoid hot-loop rehydration in class.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Failure Injection Labs\n\nActivate with:\n\n```bash\n# Simulate projector downtime\n$ make simulate_projector_outage DURATION=30s\n\n# Induce write-model crash mid-transaction\n$ make chaos_saga MODULE=payments\n```\n\nStudents then debug replay & compensating actions per the **Saga Pattern**.\n\n---\n\n## 8.     "content": "```markdown\n# EduPay Ledger Academy  \n### docs/architecture/04_saga_pattern.md\n---\n> Version: 1.3  \n> Last Reviewed: 2024-05-09  \n> Authors: Core Platform Team (@edupay-ledger)  \n> Status: \u2705 Production  \n---\n\n## 1. Why EduPay Uses the Saga Pattern\n\nEduPay processes **millions of distributed, financial micro-transactions** each semester.  \nThe platform deliberately avoids *single-phase* database transactions because:\n\n* **Micro-services** compose payments from multiple bounded contexts (Admissions, Bursar, Treasury, FX, Fraud).  \n* **Heterogeneous data stores** (PostgreSQL, Redis, EventStoreDB) participate in a single business flow.  \n* **Resiliency labs** in coursework require controlled failure injection and roll-back.  \n\nA **Saga** slices a long-running business process into a series of *local* ACID transactions plus **compensating steps**.  \nIf any step fails, the orchestrator triggers rollback actions in **reverse order**, yielding *eventual consistency* without locking global resources.\n\n```\nEnrollment_Fee \u2192 FX_Conversion \u2192 Treasury_Posting \u2192 Fraud_Scoring \u2192 Receipt_Email\n         \u2502                \u2502                \u2502              \u2502\n         \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2534\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2534\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2534\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n                       Saga Orchestrator (payment_saga.c)       \u2502\n                       \u2022 persists state in Audit_Trail          \u2502\n                       \u2022 broadcasts events over EventBus        \u2502\n                       \u2022 drives rollbacks on failure \u25c4\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n```\n\n---\n\n## 2. High-Level Flow\n\n1. **Create** a `payment_saga_t` record in the `audit_trail` stream.  \n2. **Send** `SAGA_STEP_BEGIN` for *FX_Conversion* (`fx.c`).  \n3. **Local commit** in FX; publish `SAGA_STEP_DONE`.  \n4. Orchestrator continues to *Treasury_Posting* (`ledger.c`).  \n5. If *Fraud_Scoring* fails, **publish** `SAGA_ABORT`.  \n6. Participants receiving `SAGA_ABORT` invoke *compensating* handlers.  \n7. Saga ends with `SAGA_ROLLBACK_DONE` or `SAGA_SUCCESS`.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Reference Implementation (C)\n\nAll code is kept framework-agnostic, consistent with **Clean Architecture**.  \nDependencies limited to the standard C library (`pthread` for concurrency).\n\n### 3.1. Public Interface \u2013 `include/saga.h`\n\n```c\n#ifndef EDUPAY_SAGA_H\n#define EDUPAY_SAGA_H\n\n#include <stdint.h>\n#include <stdbool.h>\n\n/* ---------- Event Bus ---------------------------------------------------- */\n\ntypedef enum {\n    EVT_SAGA_STEP_BEGIN,\n    EVT_SAGA_STEP_DONE,\n    EVT_SAGA_ABORT,\n    EVT_SAGA_ROLLBACK_DONE,\n    EVT_SAGA_SUCCESS\n} saga_event_type_t;\n\ntypedef struct {\n    saga_event_type_t type;\n    uint64_t          saga_id;\n    const char       *step_name;   /* e.g., \"FX_Conversion\" */\n    void             *payload;     /* opaque domain state   */\n} saga_event_t;\n\n/* Subscriber callback signature */\ntypedef void (*event_handler_f)(const saga_event_t *evt, void *ctx);\n\n/* Registers a handler; returns 0 on success, -1 on error */\nint eventbus_subscribe(event_handler_f cb, void *ctx);\n\n/* Broadcasts event to all subscribers; thread-safe */\nint eventbus_publish(const saga_event_t *evt);\n\n/* ---------- Saga Orchestrator ------------------------------------------- */\n\n#define SAGA_MAX_STEPS 8\n#define SAGA_STEP_NAME_MAX 32\n\ntypedef int (*saga_step_f)(uint64_t saga_id, void **payload);\ntypedef int (*saga_comp_f)(uint64_t saga_id, void *payload);\n\ntypedef struct {\n    char         name[SAGA_STEP_NAME_MAX];\n    saga_step_f  action;\n    saga_comp_f  compensate;\n} saga_step_def_t;\n\ntypedef struct {\n    uint64_t        id;\n    uint8_t         step_count;\n    uint8_t         current;\n    saga_step_def_t steps[SAGA_MAX_STEPS];\n    bool            aborted;\n} payment_saga_t;\n\n/* Initializes a saga with the supplied steps */\nvoid saga_init(payment_saga_t *saga, uint64_t id,\n               const saga_step_def_t *steps,\n               uint8_t step_count);\n\n/* Executes saga synchronously; returns 0 on success, -1 on failure */\nint saga_execute(payment_saga_t *saga);\n\n#endif /* EDUPAY_SAGA_H */\n```\n\n### 3.2. Core Implementation \u2013 `src/saga.c`\n\n```c\n#include \"saga.h\"\n#include <pthread.h>\n#include <stdio.h>\n#include <stdlib.h>\n#include <string.h>\n\n#define BUS_MAX_HANDLERS 16\n\n/* ----------------- Simple In-Process Event Bus -------------------------- */\n\ntypedef struct {\n    event_handler_f cb;\n    void           *ctx;\n} handler_entry_t;\n\nstatic handler_entry_t BUS[BUS_MAX_HANDLERS];\nstatic pthread_mutex_t BUS_LOCK = PTHREAD_MUTEX_INITIALIZER;\n\nint eventbus_subscribe(event_handler_f cb, void *ctx)\n{\n    pthread_mutex_lock(&BUS_LOCK);\n    for (int i = 0; i < BUS_MAX_HANDLERS; ++i) {\n        if (BUS[i].cb == NULL) {\n            BUS[i].cb  = cb;\n            BUS[i].ctx = ctx;\n            pthread_mutex_unlock(&BUS_LOCK);\n            return 0;\n        }\n    }\n    pthread_mutex_unlock(&BUS_LOCK);\n    return -1; /* No slots */\n}\n\nint eventbus_publish(const saga_event_t *evt)\n{\n    pthread_mutex_lock(&BUS_LOCK);\n    handler_entry_t handlers[BUS_MAX_HANDLERS];\n    memcpy(handlers, BUS, sizeof(handlers));\n    pthread_mutex_unlock(&BUS_LOCK);\n\n    for (int i = 0; i < BUS_MAX_HANDLERS; ++i) {\n        if (handlers[i].cb)\n            handlers[i].cb(evt, handlers[i].ctx);\n    }\n    return 0;\n}\n\n/* ----------------- Saga Orchestration ---------------------------------- */\n\nstatic void publish_step_event(saga_event_type_t type,\n                               const payment_saga_t *saga,\n                               const char *step_name,\n                               void *payload)\n{\n    saga_event_t evt = {\n        .type      = type,\n        .saga_id   = saga->id,\n        .step_name = step_name,\n        .payload   = payload\n    };\n    eventbus_publish(&evt);\n}\n\nvoid saga_init(payment_saga_t *s, uint64_t id,\n               const saga_step_def_t *steps,\n               uint8_t step_count)\n{\n    memset(s, 0, sizeof(*s));\n    s->id         = id;\n    s->step_count = step_count > SAGA_MAX_STEPS ? SAGA_MAX_STEPS : step_count;\n    memcpy(s->steps, steps, s->step_count * sizeof(saga_step_def_t));\n}\n\nstatic int rollback(payment_saga_t *saga)\n{\n    for (int i = saga->current; i >= 0; --i) {\n        saga_step_def_t *step = &saga->steps[i];\n        if (step->compensate) {\n            publish_step_event(EVT_SAGA_ABORT, saga, step->name, NULL);\n            if (step->compensate(saga->id, NULL) != 0)\n                fprintf(stderr, \"\u26a0  Compensation failed at %s\\n\", step->name);\n        }\n    }\n    saga_event_t done = {\n        .type      = EVT_SAGA_ROLLBACK_DONE,\n        .saga_id   = saga->id,\n        .step_name = \"ROLLBACK\"\n    };\n    eventbus_publish(&done);\n    return -1;\n}\n\nint saga_execute(payment_saga_t *saga)\n{\n    for (saga->current = 0; saga->current < saga->step_count; ++saga->current) {\n        saga_step_def_t *step = &saga->steps[saga->current];\n\n        publish_step_event(EVT_SAGA_STEP_BEGIN, saga, step->name, NULL);\n\n        void *payload = NULL;\n        if (step->action(saga->id, &payload) != 0) {\n            fprintf(stderr, \"\u274c  Saga %lu failed at step %s\\n\",\n                    saga->id, step->name);\n            saga->aborted = true;\n            return rollback(saga);\n        }\n\n        publish_step_event(EVT_SAGA_STEP_DONE, saga, step->name, payload);\n    }\n\n    saga_event_t ok = {\n        .type      = EVT_SAGA_SUCCESS,\n        .saga_id   = saga->id,\n        .step_name = \"COMPLETED\"\n    };\n    eventbus_publish(&ok);\n    return 0;\n}\n```\n\n### 3.3. Example Steps \u2013 `src/steps_fx.c`, `src/steps_ledger.c`\n\n```c\n/* src/steps_fx.c */\n#include \"saga.h\"\n#include <stdio.h>\n\nint fx_convert(uint64_t id, void **payload)\n{\n    (void)payload; /* Not needed for demo */\n    printf(\"\ud83d\udcb1  FX_Conversion performed for saga %lu\\n\", id);\n    /* simulate success */\n    return 0;\n}\n\nint fx_reverse(uint64_t id, void *payload)\n{\n    (void)payload;\n    printf(\"\u21a9  FX_Conversion reversed for saga %lu\\n\", id);\n    return 0;\n}\n```\n\n```c\n/* src/steps_ledger.c */\n#include \"saga.h\"\n#include <stdio.h>\n\nint ledger_post(uint64_t id, void **payload)\n{\n    (void)payload;\n    printf(\"\ud83d\udcd2  Ledger posting OK for saga %lu\\n\", id);\n    return 0;\n}\n\nint ledger_reverse(uint64_t id, void *payload)\n{\n    (void)payload;\n    printf(\"\u21a9  Ledger posting reversed for saga %lu\\n\", id);\n    return 0;\n}\n```\n\n### 3.4. Demonstration Driver \u2013 `samples/payment_saga.c`\n\n```c\n#include \"saga.h\"\n#include <stdio.h>\n#include <stdlib.h>\n#include <time.h>\n\n/* ---------- Step Implementations --------------------------------------- */\nextern int fx_convert(uint64_t, void **);\nextern int fx_reverse(uint64_t, void *);\n\nextern int ledger_post(uint64_t, void **);\nextern int ledger_reverse(uint64_t, void *);\n\nstatic int fraud_score(uint64_t id, void **payload)\n{\n    (void)payload;\n    printf(\"\ud83d\udd75  Fraud scoring started for saga %lu\\n\", id);\n\n    /* Simulate 30% failure rate for classroom chaos monkeys */\n    if (rand() % 10 < 3) {\n        fprintf(stderr, \"\ud83d\udea8  Fraud scoring FAILED (suspicious)\\n\");\n        return -1;\n    }\n\n    printf(\"\u2705  Fraud scoring passed\\n\");\n    return 0;\n}\n\nstatic int fraud_reverse(uint64_t id, void *payload)\n{\n    (void)payload;\n    printf(\"\u21a9  Fraud scoring compensation (unflag) for saga %lu\\n\", id);\n    return 0;\n}\n\n/* ---------- Audit Trail Console Subscriber ----------------------------- */\nstatic void audit_logger(const saga_event_t *evt, void *ctx)\n{\n    (void)ctx;\n    const char *type_str[] = {\n        \"STEP_BEGIN\", \"STEP_DONE\", \"ABORT\", \"ROLLBACK_DONE\", \"SUCCESS\"\n    };\n    printf(\"\ud83d\udcdd  Audit: %s \u2014 saga=%lu step=%s\\n\",\n           type_str[evt->type], evt->saga_id, evt->step_name);\n}\n\nint main(void)\n{\n    srand((unsigned)time(NULL));\n    eventbus_subscribe(audit_logger, NULL);\n\n    saga_step_def_t steps[] = {\n        { \"FX_Conversion\",   fx_convert,   fx_reverse   },\n        { \"Ledger_Posting\",  ledger_post,  ledger_reverse },\n        { \"Fraud_Scoring\",   fraud_score,  fraud_reverse }\n    };\n\n    payment_saga_t saga;\n    saga_init(&saga, 42, steps, 3);\n\n    int rc = saga_execute(&saga);\n    printf(rc == 0 ? \"\ud83c\udf89  Saga completed successfully!\\n\"\n                   : \"\ud83d\udc94  Saga rolled back.\\n\");\n    return rc;\n}\n```\n\nCompile & Run:\n\n```bash\ngcc -Iinclude src/saga.c src/steps_fx.c src/steps_ledger.c samples/payment_saga.c -lpthread -o bin/payment_saga\n./bin/payment_saga\n```\n\nExpected terminal output (with occasional induced failure):\n\n```\n\ud83d\udcb1  FX_Conversion performed for saga 42\n\ud83d\udcd2  Ledger posting OK for saga 42\n\ud83d\udd75  Fraud scoring started for saga 42\n\ud83d\udea8  Fraud scoring FAILED (suspicious)\n\u274c  Saga 42 failed at step Fraud_Scoring\n\u21a9  Fraud scoring compensation (unflag) for saga 42\n\u21a9  Ledger posting reversed for saga 42\n\u21a9  FX_Conversion reversed for saga 42\n\ud83d\udc94  Saga rolled back.\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Teaching Notes\n\n* The orchestrator resides **inside** the Payment bounded context, not in an external workflow engine.  \n  Code can therefore be debugged with `gdb` by novices.\n* Because the event bus is *in-process*, instructors can swap it for a\n  real Kafka / NATS adapter during advanced labs without touching business logic.\n* Compensations are **idempotent**: every reverse handler can run twice safely,\n  a mandatory property in at-least-once delivery environments.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Production Hardening Checklist\n\n- [x] Persist `payment_saga_t` progress to EventStoreDB \u2192 replay after crash.  \n- [x] Encrypt payloads (`payload_encrypt()`) for PCI-DSS compliance.  \n- [x] Emit OpenTelemetry spans for distributed tracing.  \n- [ ] Add circuit-breakers around downstream services (coming Q3).  \n\n---\n\nHappy hacking!  \nEduPay Ledger Team \u2728\n```",

    "content": "```markdown\n# 05 \u2014 Security & Compliance Architecture\nEduPay Ledger Academy (ELA) treats confidentiality, integrity, and availability as first-class\nrequirements.  Because the platform is intended both for **production payment flows** and for\n**pedagogical deep-dives**, every security control is written in C with pristine readability,\nstrong encapsulation, and complete unit-test coverage.\n\nThis document serves three audiences:\n\n1. **C-level security engineers** hardening live campus deployments.  \n2. **Professors & students** dissecting real-world fintech counter-measures.  \n3. **Auditors (PCI-DSS, SOC 2, FERPA, PSD2)** reviewing our design artifacts.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Threat Model\n\n| Asset                          | Adversary Goal                          | Mitigation                                                                             |\n| ------------------------------ | --------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |\n| Cardholder data (CHD)          | Exfiltrate PANs, CVVs, expiry dates     | Tokenization, AES-256-GCM at rest, TLS 1.3 in flight, mlock/munlock secrets            |\n| Tuition escrow accounts        | Unauthorized payout or diversion        | Dual-signature ledger, role-based ACL, multi-factor TOTP                               |\n| Student PII (FERPA)            | Deanonymize academic records            | Record-level field encryption, Attribute-based access control (ABAC)                   |\n| Audit logs                     | Tamper with or delete evidence          | Append-only Event Store, HMAC-SHA-256 chain-linking                                    |\n| Sagas (distributed txns)       | Replay or reorder compensating actions  | Idempotent command IDs, monotonic vector clocks                                        |\n\n---\n\n## 2. Regulatory Compliance Matrix\n\n| Regulation | Relevant ELA Module(s)                       | Key Controls Implemented                                                                     |\n| ---------- | -------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |\n| PCI-DSS 4  | `pci_tokenizer`, `tls_terminator`, `vault`   | PAN truncation, secure memory, quarterly ASV scans, FIPS 140-2 crypto                        |\n| PSD2       | `strong_customer_auth`, `risk_engine`        | SCA 2-factor routing, dynamic linking of transaction data                                    |\n| SOC 2 TSC  | `audit_trail`, `config_service`              | Immutable logs, least-privilege secrets rotation                                             |\n| FERPA      | `pii_encryptor`, `reporting_gateway`         | Field-level AES, consent enforcement, purpose-based de-identification                        |\n\n---\n\n## 3. Reference Implementation: PCI Tokenization Service\nThe code below is **production-ready** and compiles as a standalone library.  It demonstrates:\n\n* FIPS-compatible AES-256-GCM encryption\n* High-entropy random token generation\n* Memory-safe key handling with `mlock` + `OPENSSL_cleanse`\n* Audit-ready error codes\n\n> File location in repo: `src/security/pci_tokenizer.c`\n\n```c\n/**\n * @file pci_tokenizer.c\n *\n * Production-grade PAN tokenization compliant with PCI-DSS 4.\n *\n * Build:\n *   gcc -Wall -Wextra -Werror -pedantic -std=c11 \\\n *       pci_tokenizer.c -o libpci_tokenizer.so -fPIC -shared -lcrypto\n *\n * Author: EduPay Ledger Academy Security Team\n */\n\n#include <errno.h>\n#include <inttypes.h>\n#include <stdbool.h>\n#include <stddef.h>\n#include <stdint.h>\n#include <stdio.h>\n#include <stdlib.h>\n#include <string.h>\n#include <sys/mman.h>\n#include <unistd.h>\n\n#include <openssl/evp.h>\n#include <openssl/rand.h>\n#include <openssl/err.h>\n\n/* \u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014 Public Constants \u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014 */\n#define PCI_TOKENIZER_OK                 (0)\n#define PCI_TOKENIZER_ERR_CRYPTO        (-1)\n#define PCI_TOKENIZER_ERR_RNG           (-2)\n#define PCI_TOKENIZER_ERR_PARAM         (-3)\n#define PCI_TOKENIZER_ERR_INTERNAL      (-4)\n\n/* Always tokenise PAN down to 16 random hex chars */\n#define TOKEN_LEN_HEX                   (16)\n\n/* AES-256-GCM parameters */\n#define AES_GCM_KEY_BYTES               (32)\n#define AES_GCM_IV_BYTES                (12)\n#define AES_GCM_TAG_BYTES               (16)\n\n/* Compile-time checks */\n#if TOKEN_LEN_HEX % 2 != 0\n#   error \"TOKEN_LEN_HEX must be divisible by 2\"\n#endif\n\n/* \u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014 Secure Utilities \u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014 */\n\n/**\n * Allocate memory that is locked into RAM, never swapped to disk.\n * Returns NULL on failure.\n */\nstatic void *secure_calloc(size_t n, size_t size) {\n    size_t total = n * size;\n    void *ptr = calloc(1, total);\n    if (!ptr) return NULL;\n\n    if (mlock(ptr, total) != 0) {\n        /* Best-effort fallback: continue even if mlock fails on some OS */\n        perror(\"mlock\");\n    }\n    return ptr;\n}\n\n/**\n * Frees memory allocated by secure_calloc, wiping contents first.\n */\nstatic void secure_free(void *ptr, size_t bytes) {\n    if (!ptr) return;\n    OPENSSL_cleanse(ptr, bytes);\n    munlock(ptr, bytes);\n    free(ptr);\n}\n\n/* \u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014 Core API \u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014 */\n\n/**\n * Generates a cryptographically strong random hex string of TOKEN_LEN_HEX.\n */\nstatic int generate_token(char token_out[TOKEN_LEN_HEX + 1]) {\n    uint8_t raw[TOKEN_LEN_HEX / 2];\n    if (RAND_bytes(raw, sizeof(raw)) != 1) {\n        return PCI_TOKENIZER_ERR_RNG;\n    }\n\n    for (size_t i = 0; i < sizeof(raw); ++i)\n        sprintf(&token_out[i * 2], \"%02x\", raw[i]);\n\n    token_out[TOKEN_LEN_HEX] = '\\0';\n    return PCI_TOKENIZER_OK;\n}\n\n/**\n * Encrypts plaintext using AES-256-GCM.\n *\n * Inputs:\n *   key:        32-byte key\n *   iv:         12-byte IV\n *   plaintext:  PAN string\n *   pt_len:     plaintext length in bytes\n *\n * Outputs:\n *   ciphertext: caller-allocated buffer at least pt_len bytes\n *   tag:        16-byte authentication tag\n *   ct_len:     actual number of ciphertext bytes written\n *\n * Returns PCI_TOKENIZER_* status code.\n */\nstatic int aes256_gcm_encrypt(const uint8_t key[AES_GCM_KEY_BYTES],\n                              const uint8_t iv[AES_GCM_IV_BYTES],\n                              const uint8_t *plaintext,\n                              size_t pt_len,\n                              uint8_t *ciphertext,\n                              uint8_t tag[AES_GCM_TAG_BYTES],\n                              size_t *ct_len) {\n\n    EVP_CIPHER_CTX *ctx = EVP_CIPHER_CTX_new();\n    if (!ctx) return PCI_TOKENIZER_ERR_CRYPTO;\n\n    int len = 0;\n    int ciphertext_len = 0;\n    int ret_code = PCI_TOKENIZER_OK;\n\n    do {\n        if (EVP_EncryptInit_ex(ctx, EVP_aes_256_gcm(), NULL, NULL, NULL) != 1) {\n            ret_code = PCI_TOKENIZER_ERR_CRYPTO; break;\n        }\n        if (EVP_CIPHER_CTX_ctrl(ctx, EVP_CTRL_GCM_SET_IVLEN, AES_GCM_IV_BYTES, NULL) != 1) {\n            ret_code = PCI_TOKENIZER_ERR_CRYPTO; break;\n        }\n        if (EVP_EncryptInit_ex(ctx, NULL, NULL, key, iv) != 1) {\n            ret_code = PCI_TOKENIZER_ERR_CRYPTO; break;\n        }\n        if (EVP_EncryptUpdate(ctx, ciphertext, &len, plaintext, (int)pt_len) != 1) {\n            ret_code = PCI_TOKENIZER_ERR_CRYPTO; break;\n        }\n        ciphertext_len = len;\n        if (EVP_EncryptFinal_ex(ctx, ciphertext + len, &len) != 1) {\n            ret_code = PCI_TOKENIZER_ERR_CRYPTO; break;\n        }\n        ciphertext_len += len;\n        if (EVP_CIPHER_CTX_ctrl(ctx, EVP_CTRL_GCM_GET_TAG, AES_GCM_TAG_BYTES, tag) != 1) {\n            ret_code = PCI_TOKENIZER_ERR_CRYPTO; break;\n        }\n        *ct_len = (size_t)ciphertext_len;\n    } while (0);\n\n    EVP_CIPHER_CTX_free(ctx);\n    if (ret_code != PCI_TOKENIZER_OK)\n        ERR_print_errors_fp(stderr);\n\n    return ret_code;\n}\n\n/* \u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014 Public Facade \u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014 */\n\n/**\n * Tokenises a Primary Account Number (PAN).\n *\n * The caller supplies:\n *   pan                 PAN string (digits only)\n *\n * The library returns:\n *   out_token           TOKEN_LEN_HEX-char hex string\n *   out_ciphertext      Encrypted PAN (malloc'd, must be free()'d by caller)\n *   out_ciphertext_len  Length of encrypted PAN\n *   out_iv              12-byte IV\n *   out_tag             16-byte GCM tag\n *\n * Note: the encryption key is managed by the HSM module; for demo purposes\n *       we generate a random key here and return it to the caller.\n */\nint pci_tokenize_pan(const char  *pan,\n                     char        out_token[TOKEN_LEN_HEX + 1],\n                     uint8_t   **out_ciphertext,\n                     size_t     *out_ciphertext_len,\n                     uint8_t     out_iv[AES_GCM_IV_BYTES],\n                     uint8_t     out_tag[AES_GCM_TAG_BYTES],\n                     uint8_t     out_key[AES_GCM_KEY_BYTES]) {\n\n    if (!pan || !out_token || !out_ciphertext || !out_ciphertext_len ||\n        !out_iv || !out_tag || !out_key) {\n        return PCI_TOKENIZER_ERR_PARAM;\n    }\n\n    size_t pan_len = strlen(pan);\n    if (pan_len == 0 || pan_len > 32) { /* 19 digits + possible separators */\n        return PCI_TOKENIZER_ERR_PARAM;\n    }\n\n    /* Step 1: generate random token */\n    int rc = generate_token(out_token);\n    if (rc != PCI_TOKENIZER_OK) return rc;\n\n    /* Step 2: generate fresh AES GCM key & IV */\n    if (RAND_bytes(out_key, AES_GCM_KEY_BYTES) != 1) {\n        return PCI_TOKENIZER_ERR_RNG;\n    }\n    if (RAND_bytes(out_iv, AES_GCM_IV_BYTES) != 1) {\n        return PCI_TOKENIZER_ERR_RNG;\n    }\n\n    /* Step 3: secure memory allocation for ciphertext */\n    *out_ciphertext = malloc(pan_len); /* ciphertext length equals plaintext */\n    if (!*out_ciphertext) {\n        return PCI_TOKENIZER_ERR_INTERNAL;\n    }\n\n    /* Step 4: encrypt PAN */\n    rc = aes256_gcm_encrypt(out_key,\n                            out_iv,\n                            (const uint8_t *)pan,\n                            pan_len,\n                            *out_ciphertext,\n                            out_tag,\n                            out_ciphertext_len);\n\n    if (rc != PCI_TOKENIZER_OK) {\n        OPENSSL_cleanse(*out_ciphertext, pan_len);\n        free(*out_ciphertext);\n        *out_ciphertext = NULL;\n        *out_ciphertext_len = 0;\n        return rc;\n    }\n\n    return PCI_TOKENIZER_OK;\n}\n\n/**\n * Wipes and frees the ciphertext buffer returned by pci_tokenize_pan().\n */\nvoid pci_tokenizer_free_ciphertext(uint8_t *ciphertext, size_t len) {\n    if (!ciphertext) return;\n    OPENSSL_cleanse(ciphertext, len);\n    free(ciphertext);\n}\n\n/* \u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014 Example Usage \u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014\u2014 */\n#ifdef PCI_TOKENIZER_DEMO_MAIN\nint main(void) {\n    const char *pan = \"4111111111111111\";\n    char token[TOKEN_LEN_HEX + 1];\n\n    uint8_t *ciphertext = NULL;\n    size_t   ciphertext_len = 0;\n    uint8_t  iv[AES_GCM_IV_BYTES];\n    uint8_t  tag[AES_GCM_TAG_BYTES];\n    uint8_t  key[AES_GCM_KEY_BYTES];\n\n    int rc = pci_tokenize_pan(pan, token, &ciphertext, &ciphertext_len,\n                              iv, tag, key);\n    if (rc != PCI_TOKENIZER_OK) {\n        fprintf(stderr, \"Tokenization failed (err=%d)\\n\", rc);\n        return EXIT_FAILURE;\n    }\n\n    printf(\"PAN           : %s\\n\", pan);\n    printf(\"Token         : %s\\n\", token);\n    printf(\"Ciphertext    : \");\n    for (size_t i = 0; i < ciphertext_len; ++i)\n        printf(\"%02x\", ciphertext[i]);\n    printf(\"\\n\");\n\n    /* Proper key handling omitted for brevity \u2014 would be escrowed in HSM. */\n    pci_tokenizer_free_ciphertext(ciphertext, ciphertext_len);\n    OPENSSL_cleanse(key, sizeof(key));\n    return EXIT_SUCCESS;\n}\n#endif\n```\n\n### Unit Test Snippet\n\n```c\n#include \"pci_tokenizer.h\"\n#include <assert.h>\n\nvoid test_token_length(void) {\n    char token[TOKEN_LEN_HEX + 1];\n    /* ... invoke tokenizer ... */\n    assert(strlen(token) == TOKEN_LEN_HEX);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4.            uint8_t       *out_cipher,\n                size_t         out_cipher_sz);\n\n/**\n * Decrypts and authenticates a buffer produced by cg_seal().\n *\n * Returns number of plaintext bytes or                    */\n/* ------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n/* Overwrite |len| bytes starting at |ptr| even under aggressive optimisation */\nvoid cg_secure_bzero(void *ptr, size_t len);\n\n/* ------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/*  Key management (teaching mode)                                           */\n/* ------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n/**\n * Acquires an AES-256-GCM key.\n *   \u2022 Production:  pulled from HSM via PKCS#11.\n *   \u2022 Lab 12u\n#define CG_AES_GCM_TAG_LEN  16u\n#define CG_PAN_MAX_LEN      19u     /* ISO/IEC 7812-1 */\n#define CG_TOKEN_LEN        19u\n\nstruct cg_key { uint8_t key[32]; };\n\n/* cg_generate_iv(uint8_t *iv, size_t iv_len)\n{\n    return RAND_bytes(iv, (int)iv_len) == 1 ? 0 : -EIO;\n}\n\nstatic int cg_validate_luhn(const char *digits)\n{\n    size_t len = strlen(digits);\n    int sum = 0, alt = 0;\n\n    for (ssize_t i = (ssize_t)len - 1; i >= 0; --i)\n    {\n        int d = digits[i] - '0';\n        if (d < 0 || d > 9) return -EINVAL;\n        if (alt) { d *= 2; if (d > 9) d -= 9; }\n        sum += d; alt = !alt;\n    }\n    return sum % 10 == 0 ? 0 : -EINVAL;\n}\n\nstatic uint8_t cg_rand_digit(void)\n{\n    uint8_t b; RAND_bytes(&b, 1); return (uint8_t)(b % 10);\n}\n\nstatic int cg_build_token(const char *pan, char *tok)\n{\n    size_t len = strlen(pan);\n    if (len < 8 || len > CG_PAN_MAX_LEN) return -EINVAL;\n\n    memcpy(tok, pan, 6);                 /* Keep BIN for analytics */\n    for (size_t i = 6; i < len - 1; ++i) /* Randomise body         */\n        tok[i] = '0' + cg_rand_digit();\n\n    /* Recalculate Luhn check digit */\n    int sum = 0, alt = 1;\n    for (ssize_t i = (ssize_t)len - 2; i >= 0; --i)\n    {\n        int d = tok[i] - '0';\n        if (alt) { d *= 2; if (d > 9) d -= 9; }\n        sum += d; alt = !alt;\n    }\n    tok[len - 1] = '0' + ((10 - (sum % 10)) % 10);\n    tok[len] = '\\0';\n    return 0;\n}\n\n/* \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500 Public API \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500 */\n\nint cg_tokenise_pan(const char *pan, char *out_token, size_t out_len)\n{\n    if (!pan || !out_token)                 return -EINVAL;\n    const size_t n = strlen(pan);\n    if (n == 0 || n > CG_PAN_MAX_LEN)       return -EINVAL;\n    if (out_len < n + 1)                    return -ENOSPC;\n    if (cg_validate_luhn(pan) != 0)         return -EINVAL;\n\n    /* Switchable algorithm for /* Fallback path */\n    }\n    return cg_build_token(pan, out_token);\n}\n\nssize_t cg_seal(cg_key_t      *key,\n                const uint8_t *pt,\n                size_t         pt_len,\n                uint8_t       *out,\n                size_t         out_sz)\n{\n    if (!key || !pt || !out || pt_len == 0)  return -EINVAL;\n    const size_t need = CG_AES_GCM_IV_LEN + pt_len + CG_AES_GCM_TAG_LEN;\n    if (out_sz < need)                       return -ENOSPC;\n\n    uint8_t *iv     = out;\n    uint8_t *cipher = out + CG_AES_GCM_IV_LEN;\n    uint8_t *tag    = cipher + pt_len;\n\n    if (cg_generate_iv(iv, CG_AES_GCM_IV_LEN) != 0) return -EIO;\n\n    ssize_t ret = -EIO;\n    EVP_CIPHER_CTX *ctx = EVP_CIPHER_CTX_new();\n    if (!ctx) return -ENOMEM;\n\n    do {\n        if (EVP_EncryptInit_ex(ctx, EVP_aes_256_gcm(), NULL, NULL, NULL) != 1) break;\n        if (EVP_CIPHER_CTX_ctrl(ctx, EVP_CTRL_GCM_SET_IVLEN,\n                                CG_AES_GCM_IV_LEN, NULL) != 1)               break;\n        if (EVP_EncryptInit_ex(ctx, NULL, NULL, key->key, iv) != 1)           break;\n\n        int len = 0, total = 0;\n        if (EVP_EncryptUpdate(ctx, cipher, &len, pt, (int)pt_len) != 1)       break;\n        total += len;\n        if (EVP_EncryptFinal_ex(ctx, cipher + total, &len) != 1)              break;\n        total += len;\n        if (EVP_CIPHER_CTX_ctrl(ctx, EVP_CTRL_GCM_GET_TAG,\n                                CG_AES_GCM_TAG_LEN, tag) != 1)               break;\n\n        ret = CG_AES_GCM_IV_LEN + total + CG_AES_GCM_TAG_LEN;\n    } while (0);\n\n    EVP_CIPHER_CTX_free(ctx);\n    return ret;\n}\n\nssize_t cg_open(cg_key_t      *key,\n                const uint8_t *in,\n                size_t         in_len,\n                uint8_t       *out,\n                size_t         out_sz)\n{\n    if (!key || !in || !out)                         return -EINVAL;\n    if (in_len < CG_AES_GCM_IV_LEN + CG_AES_GCM_TAG_LEN) return -EINVAL;\n\n    const uint8_t *iv     = in;\n    const uint8_t *cipher = in + CG_AES_GCM_IV_LEN;\n    const size_t   ct_len = in_len - CG_AES_GCM_IV_LEN - CG_AES_GCM_TAG_LEN;\n    const uint8_t *tag    = in + in_len - CG_AES_GCM_TAG_LEN;\n\n    if (out_sz < ct_len)                             return -ENOSPC;\n\n    ssize_t ret = -EIO;\n    EVP_CIPHER_CTX *ctx = EVP_CIPHER_CTX_new();\n    if (!ctx) return -ENOMEM;\n\n    do {\n        if (EVP_DecryptInit_ex(ctx, EVP_aes_256_gcm(), NULL, NULL, NULL) != 1) break;\n        if (EVP_CIPHER_CTX_ctrl(ctx, EVP_CTRL_GCM_SET_IVLEN,\n                                CG_AES_GCM_IV_LEN, NULL) != 1)               break;\n        if (EVP_DecryptInit_ex(ctx, NULL, NULL, key->key, iv) != 1)           break;\n\n        int len = 0, total = 0;\n        if (EVP_DecryptUpdate(ctx, out, &len, cipher, (int)ct_len) != 1)      break;\n        total += len;\n\n        if (EVP_CIPHER_CTX_ctrl(ctx, EVP_CTRL_GCM_SET_TAG,\n                                CG_AES_GCM_TAG_LEN, (void *)tag) != 1)       break;\n        if (EVP_DecryptFinal_ex(ctx, out + total, &len) != 1) {\n            ret = -EBADMSG;                                                  break;\n        }\n        total += len;\n        ret = total;\n    } while (0);\n\n    EVP_CIPHER_CTX_free(ctx);\n    return ret;\n}\n\nvoid cg_secure_bzero(void *ptr, size_t len)\n{\n    if (!ptr || !len) return;\n#if defined(__STDC_LIB_EXT1__)\n    memset_s(ptr, len, 0, len);\n#else\n    volatile uint8_t *p = (volatile uint8_t *)ptr;\n    while (len--) *p++ = 0;\n#endif\n}\n\ncg_key_t *cg_key_acquire(void)\n{\n    cg_key_t *k = calloc(1, sizeof *k);\n    if (!k) return NULL;\n\n    const char *env = getenv(\"EDUPAY_COMPLIANCE_KEY\");\n    if (env && strlen(env) == 64)\n    {   /* Hex-decode deterministic, instructor-supplied key */\n        for (size_t i = 0; i < 32; ++i)\n            sscanf(&env[i * 2], \"%2hhx\", &k->key[i]);\n    }\n    else if (RAND_bytes(k->key, sizeof k->key) != 1)\n    {\n        free(k); k = NULL;\n    }\n    return k;\n}\n\nvoid cg_key_release(cg_key_t *key)\n{\n    if (!key) return;\n    cg_secure_bzero(key->key, sizeof key->key);\n    free(key);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3 \u2571 4\u2003End-to-end console demo (`example_usage.c`)\n\n```c\n/* Compile with\n *   cc -std=c11 -Wall -Wextra example_usage.c compliance_guard.c -lcrypto -o fprintf(stderr, \"Decryption failed: %zd\\n\", n_plain);\n        return 1;\n    }\n    printf(\"Decrypted token: %.*s\\n\", (int)n_plain, clear);\n    cg_secure_bzero(clear, (size_t)n_plain);\n\n
